	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading">List of US Open men's singles champions</h1>
	<div id="bodyContent" class="vector-body">
		<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
		<div id="contentSub"></div>
		<div id="contentSub2"></div>
		
		<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_US_Open_men%27s_singles_champions#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_US_Open_men%27s_singles_champions#searchInput">Jump to search</a>
		<div id="mw-content-text" class="mw-body-content mw-content-ltr" lang="en" dir="ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Wikimedia list article</div>
<table class="infobox"><caption class="infobox-title">US Open Men's Singles Champions</caption><tbody><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Location</th><td class="infobox-data"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Flushing_Meadows%E2%80%93Corona_Park" title="Flushing MeadowsCorona Park">Flushing Meadows</a>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Queens" title="Queens">Queens</a> <br> New York City<br>United States</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Venue</th><td class="infobox-data"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/USTA_Billie_Jean_King_National_Tennis_Center" title="USTA Billie Jean King National Tennis Center">USTA Billie Jean King National Tennis Center</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Governing body</th><td class="infobox-data"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/USTA" class="mw-redirect" title="USTA">USTA</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Created</th><td class="infobox-data">1881<span class="noprint">; background:#B2C8FF; color:black;">Most titles</th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Amateur era</th><td class="infobox-data"><b>7</b>: <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Richard_Sears_(tennis)" title="Richard Sears (tennis)">Richard Sears</a><br><b>7</b>:  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/William_Larned" title="William Larned">William Larned</a><br><b>7</b>: <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bill_Tilden" title="Bill Tilden">Bill Tilden</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Open era</th><td class="infobox-data"><b>5</b>: <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jimmy_Connors" title="Jimmy Connors">Jimmy Connors</a><br><b>5</b>: <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pete_Sampras" title="Pete Sampras">Pete Sampras</a><br><b>5</b>: <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roger_Federer" title="Roger Federer">Roger Federer</a></td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" class="infobox-header" style="text-align:center; background:#B2C8FF; color:black;">Current champion</th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" class="infobox-full-data"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Daniil_Medvedev" title="Daniil Medvedev">Daniil Medvedev</a><br>(First title)</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The <b>US Open men's singles championship</b> is an annual <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tennis" title="Tennis">tennis</a> tournament that is part of the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/US_Open_(tennis)" title="US Open (tennis)">US Open</a><sup id="cite_ref-name_5-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_US_Open_men%27s_singles_champions#cite_note-name-5">[c]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-openera_8-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_US_Open_men%27s_singles_champions#cite_note-openera-8">[d]</a></sup> and was established in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1881_U.S._National_Championships_(tennis)" title="1881 U.S. National Championships (tennis)">1881</a>. It is played on <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tennis_court#Hard_courts" title="Tennis court">outdoor hard courts</a><sup id="cite_ref-hardcourt_10-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_US_Open_men%27s_singles_champions#cite_note-hardcourt-10">[e]</a></sup> at the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/USTA_Billie_Jean_King_National_Tennis_Center" title="USTA Billie Jean King National Tennis Center">USTA Billie Jean King National Tennis Center</a> in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Flushing_Meadows_%E2%80%93_Corona_Park" class="mw-redirect" title="Flushing Meadows  Corona Park">Flushing Meadows  Corona Park</a>, New York City, United States.<sup id="cite_ref-USOProfile_11-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_US_Open_men%27s_singles_champions#cite_note-USOProfile-11">[6]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-2008USOHistory_3-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_US_Open_men%27s_singles_champions#cite_note-2008USOHistory-3">[1]</a></sup>The US Open is played during a two-week period in late August and early September, and has been chronologically the last of the four <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grand_Slam_(tennis)" title="Grand Slam (tennis)">Grand Slam</a> tournaments of the tennis <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Season_(sports)" title="Season (sports)">season</a> since 1987.<sup id="cite_ref-2008USOFinals_6-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_US_Open_men%27s_singles_champions#cite_note-2008USOFinals-6">[3]</a></sup> <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Newport,_Rhode_Island" title="Newport, Rhode Island">Newport</a> (18811914), <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Forest_Hills,_Queens" title="Forest Hills, Queens">Forest Hills</a> (19151920, 19241977), and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philadelphia" title="Philadelphia">Philadelphia</a> (19211923) held the event before it settled in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1978_US_Open_(tennis)" title="1978 US Open (tennis)">1978</a> at the USTA National Tennis Center, now the USTA Billie Jean King National Tennis Center, in New York City.<sup id="cite_ref-USTAFinals_4-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_US_Open_men%27s_singles_champions#cite_note-USTAFinals-4">[2]</a></sup> The inaugural tournament, in 1881, was reserved for <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Tennis_Association" title="United States Tennis Association">United States National Lawn Tennis Association</a> (USNLTA) club members, before the championships opened to international competitors in 1882.<sup id="cite_ref-2008USOHistory_3-2" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_US_Open_men%27s_singles_champions#cite_note-2008USOHistory-3">[1]</a></sup>  The <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Tennis_Association" title="United States Tennis Association">USTA</a> is the national body that organizes this event.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=List_of_US_Open_men%27s_singles_champions&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The men's singles' rules have undergone several changes since the first edition. From <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1884_U.S._National_Championships_(tennis)" title="1884 U.S. National Championships (tennis)">1884</a> to <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1911_U.S._National_Championships_(tennis)" title="1911 U.S. National Championships (tennis)">1911</a>, the event started with a <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Single-elimination_tournament" title="Single-elimination tournament">knockout</a> phase, the All-Comers singles, whose winner faced the defending champion in a <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_tennis#Challenge_Round" class="mw-redirect" title="Glossary of tennis">challenge round</a>. The All-Comers winner was awarded the title six times (<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1888_U.S._National_Championships_(tennis)" title="1888 U.S. National Championships (tennis)">1888</a>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1893_U.S._National_Championships_(tennis)" title="1893 U.S. National Championships (tennis)">1893</a>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1898_U.S._National_Championships_(tennis)" title="1898 U.S. National Championships (tennis)">1898</a>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1901_U.S._National_Championships_(tennis)" title="1901 U.S. National Championships (tennis)">1901</a>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1904_U.S._National_Championships_(tennis)" title="1904 U.S. National Championships (tennis)">1904</a>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1907_U.S._National_Championships_(tennis)" title="1907 U.S. National Championships (tennis)">1907</a>) in the absence of the previous year's champion. The challenge round system was abolished with the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1912_U.S._National_Championships_(tennis)" title="1912 U.S. National Championships (tennis)">1912</a> edition.<sup id="cite_ref-Talbert_12-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_US_Open_men%27s_singles_champions#cite_note-Talbert-12">[7]</a></sup> From 1908 to 1914, when the championships were held at Newport, men's singles draws had exceeded 128 players,<sup id="cite_ref-Talbert_12-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_US_Open_men%27s_singles_champions#cite_note-Talbert-12">[7]</a></sup> but when the event moved to Forest Hills in 1915 entries would be "submitted by clubs, thereby making the clubs weed out mediocre players.  Furthermore, the entry fee would be set high enough to prevent cheapskates from entering just to get a seat at the tournament at a lower price and then defaulting".<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_US_Open_men%27s_singles_champions#cite_note-13">[8]</a></sup> Since 1881, all matches but the All-Comers final and the challenge round were played as the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tennis_score#Scoring_a_set" class="mw-redirect" title="Tennis score">best-of-three sets</a>, before the event switched to <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tennis_score#Scoring_a_set" class="mw-redirect" title="Tennis score">best-of-five</a> for all rounds in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1886_U.S._National_Championships_(tennis)" title="1886 U.S. National Championships (tennis)">1886</a>. Best-two-out-of-three-sets matches were reintroduced for early rounds in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1917_U.S._National_Championships" class="mw-redirect" title="1917 U.S. National Championships">1917</a>, from <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1943_U.S._National_Championships" class="mw-redirect" title="1943 U.S. National Championships">1943</a> to <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1945_U.S._National_Championships" class="mw-redirect" title="1945 U.S. National Championships">1945</a>, and from <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1975_US_Open_(tennis)" title="1975 US Open (tennis)">1975</a> to <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1978_US_Open_(tennis)" title="1978 US Open (tennis)">1978</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Talbert_12-2" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_US_Open_men%27s_singles_champions#cite_note-Talbert-12">[7]</a></sup> Before <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1884_U.S._National_Championships" class="mw-redirect" title="1884 U.S. National Championships">1884</a>, the winner of the next game at five-games<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_tennis#All" class="mw-redirect" title="Glossary of tennis">all</a> took the set in every match except the All-Comers final and the challenge round, which were won by the player who had at least six games and at least two games more than his opponent. This <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_tennis#Advantage_format" class="mw-redirect" title="Glossary of tennis">advantage format</a> was introduced for the final sets of early rounds in 1884, and used for all sets in all rounds from 1887 to <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1969_US_Open_(tennis)" title="1969 US Open (tennis)">1969</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Talbert_12-3" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_US_Open_men%27s_singles_champions#cite_note-Talbert-12">[7]</a></sup> The <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tennis_score#Scoring_a_tiebreak_game" class="mw-redirect" title="Tennis score">tie-break</a> system was introduced in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1970_US_Open_(tennis)" title="1970 US Open (tennis)">1970</a> for all sets, in its best-of-nine points <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_tennis#Sudden_Death" class="mw-redirect" title="Glossary of tennis">sudden death</a> version until <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1974_US_Open_(tennis)" title="1974 US Open (tennis)">1974</a>, and in its best-of-13 points <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_tennis#Lingering_Death" class="mw-redirect" title="Glossary of tennis">lingering death</a> version since <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1975_US_Open_(tennis)" title="1975 US Open (tennis)">1975</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Talbert_12-4" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_US_Open_men%27s_singles_champions#cite_note-Talbert-12">[7]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-2008USOYearbyyear_7-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_US_Open_men%27s_singles_champions#cite_note-2008USOYearbyyear-7">[4]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-SuddenLingering_14-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_US_Open_men%27s_singles_champions#cite_note-SuddenLingering-14">[9]</a></sup> In addition, the US Open was the first slam to have a fifth set tie-break.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_US_Open_men%27s_singles_champions#cite_note-15">[10]</a></sup>
</p><p>The court surface changed twice, from <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tennis_court#Grass_courts" title="Tennis court">grass</a> (18811974), to <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tennis_court#Clay_courts" title="Tennis court">Har-Tru clay</a> (19751977), to <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tennis_court#Hard_courts" title="Tennis court">DecoTurf hard</a> courts, since 1978.<sup id="cite_ref-Surfaces_16-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_US_Open_men%27s_singles_champions#cite_note-Surfaces-16">[11]</a></sup>  The only man to win on all three surfaces, which are grass, Har-Tru clay, and DecoTurf hard was <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jimmy_Connors" title="Jimmy Connors">Jimmy Connors</a>.
</p><p>The champion receives a full-size replica of the event's trophy engraved with his name.<sup id="cite_ref-FedererTrophy_17-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_US_Open_men%27s_singles_champions#cite_note-FedererTrophy-17">[12]</a></sup> In 2010, the winner received prize money of US$1,700,000.<sup id="cite_ref-2009USOPrizeMoney_18-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_US_Open_men%27s_singles_champions#cite_note-2009USOPrizeMoney-18">[13]</a></sup> A bonus pool of $1,000,000 is also to US Open champions who have clinched the first place of the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/US_Open_Series" title="US Open Series">US Open Series</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-USOSeries_19-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_US_Open_men%27s_singles_champions#cite_note-USOSeries-19">[14]</a></sup>
</p><p>In the U.S. National Championships, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Richard_Sears_(tennis)" title="Richard Sears (tennis)">Richard Sears</a> (18811887), <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/William_Larned" title="William Larned">William Larned</a> (19011902, 19071911) and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bill_Tilden" title="Bill Tilden">Bill Tilden</a> (19201925, 1929) hold the record for most titles in the men's singles, with seven victories each. Four of Sears' wins and all of Larned's, came within the challenge round format, and they won respectively only thrice and twice after going through a complete draw. Sears also holds the all-time record for most consecutive titles, with seven from (1881 to 1887); the first win came when the event was closed to foreign participants. Without the challenge round, the record stands at six, and is held by Tilden (19201925).<sup id="cite_ref-2008USOFinals_6-2" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_US_Open_men%27s_singles_champions#cite_note-2008USOFinals-6">[3]</a></sup>
</p><p>During the US Open, since the inclusion of the professional tennis players, Jimmy Connors (1974, 1976, 1978, 19821983), <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pete_Sampras" title="Pete Sampras">Pete Sampras</a> (1990, 1993, 19951996, 2002), and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roger_Federer" title="Roger Federer">Roger Federer</a> (20042008) have won the most championships, with five titles.  Federer has had the most consecutive wins, with five (20042008).<sup id="cite_ref-2008USOFinals_6-3" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_US_Open_men%27s_singles_champions#cite_note-2008USOFinals-6">[3]</a></sup>
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="U.S._National_Championships">U.S. National Championships</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=List_of_US_Open_men%27s_singles_champions&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: U.S. National Championships">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Richard_Sears_(1880s)_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="./List of US Open men&#39;s singles champions - Wikipedia_files/Richard_Sears_(1880s)_(cropped).jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="240" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Richard_Sears_%281880s%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/300px-Richard_Sears_%281880s%29_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Richard_Sears_%281880s%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/400px-Richard_Sears_%281880s%29_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1421" data-file-height="1706"></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Richard_Sears_(1880s)_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Richard_Sears_(tennis)" title="Richard Sears (tennis)">Richard Sears</a>, the champion of the first seven editions of the U.S Championships.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:William_Augustus_Larned_crop.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A man in white pants and shirt swings a wooden racket on a grass court, with other male and female tennis players in the background" src="./List of US Open men&#39;s singles champions - Wikipedia_files/200px-William_Augustus_Larned_crop.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/William_Augustus_Larned_crop.jpg/300px-William_Augustus_Larned_crop.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/William_Augustus_Larned_crop.jpg/400px-William_Augustus_Larned_crop.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1365" data-file-height="2000"></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:William_Augustus_Larned_crop.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/William_Larned" title="William Larned">William Larned</a> was the second man to win seven titles at the event.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Bill_Tilden_in_color.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A man turned sideways and swinging a tennis racket" src="./List of US Open men&#39;s singles champions - Wikipedia_files/200px-Bill_Tilden_in_color.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="328" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/23/Bill_Tilden_in_color.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="265" data-file-height="434"></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Bill_Tilden_in_color.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Tilden won six consecutive titles and seven non-<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_tennis#Challenge_Round" class="mw-redirect" title="Glossary of tennis">challenge round</a> championships in total, an all-time record.</div></div></div>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="US_Open">US Open</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=List_of_US_Open_men%27s_singles_champions&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: US Open">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Jimmy_Connors_2_(1978).jpg" class="image"><img alt="A brown-haired man dressed in a white shirt swings a two-handed backhand" src="./List of US Open men&#39;s singles champions - Wikipedia_files/170px-Jimmy_Connors_2_(1978).jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="248" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Jimmy_Connors_2_%281978%29.jpg/255px-Jimmy_Connors_2_%281978%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Jimmy_Connors_2_%281978%29.jpg/340px-Jimmy_Connors_2_%281978%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1856" data-file-height="2706"></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Jimmy_Connors_2_(1978).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jimmy_Connors" title="Jimmy Connors">Jimmy Connors</a> won the US Open five times on three different surfaces.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:John_McEnroe_(1979)-2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="American John McEnroe at the 1979 ABN Tennis Tournament in Rotterdam" src="./List of US Open men&#39;s singles champions - Wikipedia_files/170px-John_McEnroe_(1979)-2.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="232" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/John_McEnroe_%281979%29-2.jpg/255px-John_McEnroe_%281979%29-2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/John_McEnroe_%281979%29-2.jpg/340px-John_McEnroe_%281979%29-2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="416" data-file-height="567"></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:John_McEnroe_(1979)-2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_McEnroe" title="John McEnroe">John McEnroe</a> won four of his seven <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grand_Slam_(tennis)" title="Grand Slam (tennis)">Majors</a> at the US Open.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Pete_Sampras.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A black-haired man in white shorts and a white shirt prepares to serve with a modern racket" src="./List of US Open men&#39;s singles champions - Wikipedia_files/170px-Pete_Sampras.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Pete_Sampras.jpg/255px-Pete_Sampras.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Pete_Sampras.jpg/340px-Pete_Sampras.jpg 2x" data-file-width="667" data-file-height="1000"></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Pete_Sampras.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pete_Sampras" title="Pete Sampras">Pete Sampras</a> captured five titles in New York City.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Roger_Federer_-_US_Open_2006.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A brown-haired male tennis player with white shorts, a blue shirt and a blue headband swings a right-handed forehand on a hard court surface" src="./List of US Open men&#39;s singles champions - Wikipedia_files/170px-Roger_Federer_-_US_Open_2006.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Roger_Federer_-_US_Open_2006.jpg/255px-Roger_Federer_-_US_Open_2006.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Roger_Federer_-_US_Open_2006.jpg/340px-Roger_Federer_-_US_Open_2006.jpg 2x" data-file-width="683" data-file-height="1024"></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Roger_Federer_-_US_Open_2006.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roger_Federer" title="Roger Federer">Roger Federer</a> won an <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_tennis#Open_Era" title="History of tennis">Open Era</a> record of five consecutive titles between 2004 and 2008.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Rafael_Nadal_at_the_2010_US_Open_01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A brown-haired male tennis player with black shorts, a green shirt and a black headband swings a left-handed backhand on a hard court surface" src="./List of US Open men&#39;s singles champions - Wikipedia_files/170px-Rafael_Nadal_at_the_2010_US_Open_01.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="113" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Rafael_Nadal_at_the_2010_US_Open_01.jpg/255px-Rafael_Nadal_at_the_2010_US_Open_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Rafael_Nadal_at_the_2010_US_Open_01.jpg/340px-Rafael_Nadal_at_the_2010_US_Open_01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1937" data-file-height="1291"></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Rafael_Nadal_at_the_2010_US_Open_01.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rafael_Nadal" title="Rafael Nadal">Rafael Nadal</a> captured four titles in the 2010s decade.</div></div></div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=List_of_US_Open_men%27s_singles_champions&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1011085734">.mw-parser-output .reflist{font-size:90%;margin-bottom:0.5em;list-style-type:decimal}.mw-parser-output .reflist .references{font-size:100%;margin-bottom:0;list-style-type:inherit}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-2{column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-3{column-width:25em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns{margin-top:0.3em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns ol{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns li{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-alpha{list-style-type:upper-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-roman{list-style-type:upper-roman}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-alpha{list-style-type:lower-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-greek{list-style-type:lower-greek}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-roman{list-style-type:lower-roman}</style><div class="reflist reflist-lower-alpha">
<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-clay-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_US_Open_men%27s_singles_champions#cite_ref-clay_1-0" aria-label="Jump up" title="Jump up">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Played on HarTru surface.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-hard-2"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_US_Open_men%27s_singles_champions#cite_ref-hard_2-0" aria-label="Jump up" title="Jump up">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Played on DecoTurf surface.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-name-5"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_US_Open_men%27s_singles_champions#cite_ref-name_5-0" aria-label="Jump up" title="Jump up">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Known as the <i>U.S. National Championships</i> during the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_tennis" title="History of tennis">Amateur Era</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-2008USOHistory_3-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_US_Open_men%27s_singles_champions#cite_note-2008USOHistory-3">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-USTAFinals_4-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_US_Open_men%27s_singles_champions#cite_note-USTAFinals-4">[2]</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-openera-8"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_US_Open_men%27s_singles_champions#cite_ref-openera_8-0"><span class="cite-accessibility-label">Jump up to: </span><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_US_Open_men%27s_singles_champions#cite_ref-openera_8-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">The tournament entered the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_tennis#Open_Era" title="History of tennis">Open Era</a> with the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1968_US_Open_(tennis)" title="1968 US Open (tennis)">1968</a> edition, allowing <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Professional" title="Professional">professional</a> players to compete alongside <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amateur" title="Amateur">amateurs</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-2008USOFinals_6-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_US_Open_men%27s_singles_champions#cite_note-2008USOFinals-6">[3]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-2008USOYearbyyear_7-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_US_Open_men%27s_singles_champions#cite_note-2008USOYearbyyear-7">[4]</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-hardcourt-10"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_US_Open_men%27s_singles_champions#cite_ref-hardcourt_10-0" aria-label="Jump up" title="Jump up">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The US Open specifically uses <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/DecoTurf" title="DecoTurf">DecoTurf</a> hard courts, categorized as a "Medium" speed surface by the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Tennis_Federation" title="International Tennis Federation">International Tennis Federation</a> (ITF).<sup id="cite_ref-Decoturf_9-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_US_Open_men%27s_singles_champions#cite_note-Decoturf-9">[5]</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-national-21"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_US_Open_men%27s_singles_champions#cite_ref-national_21-0" aria-label="Jump up" title="Jump up">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1917_U.S._National_Championships_(tennis)" title="1917 U.S. National Championships (tennis)">1917 U.S. National Championships</a>, taking place during World War I, were held as a <i>National Patriotic Tournament</i> awarding no prize to the winner.<sup id="cite_ref-National_20-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_US_Open_men%27s_singles_champions#cite_note-National-20">[15]</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-22"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_US_Open_men%27s_singles_champions#cite_ref-22" aria-label="Jump up" title="Jump up">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Each year is linked to an article about that particular event's draw.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-tiebreak-23"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_US_Open_men%27s_singles_champions#cite_ref-tiebreak_23-0" aria-label="Jump up" title="Jump up">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In 1970, 1971 and 1972 tiebreaks were "five point tiebreaks".</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-tch-24"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_US_Open_men%27s_singles_champions#cite_ref-tch_24-0" aria-label="Jump up" title="Jump up">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Czechoslovakia" title="Czechoslovakia">Czechoslovakia</a> (TCH, 19181992), evolved into <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Czech_Republic" title="Czech Republic">Czech Republic</a> (CZE, 1992present) and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Slovakia" title="Slovakia">Slovakia</a> (SVK, 1992present).</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-ger-25"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_US_Open_men%27s_singles_champions#cite_ref-ger_25-0" aria-label="Jump up" title="Jump up">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">One win by a player from <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/West_Germany" title="West Germany">West Germany</a> (FRG, 19491990).</span>
</li>
</ol></div></div>
